# SDD index

Reserved slots for the foundation phase (PRs 1–10) per the Plan-agent
macro-arc (info-hub `raw/dumps/2026-05-16-sovereign-os-macro-arc-plan.md`).
Numbering is three-digit zero-padded, never recycled.

**Status vocabulary** (the `Status` column): `draft` (proposed / in design), `review`
(spec reviewed, pending gate), `scoping` (decision package, operator decision pending),
`accepted` (design decided), `active` (implementation in progress), `complete` (shipped +
verified). The provenance column names the authoring session, not an ephemeral branch —
`tests/lint/test_sdd_index_hygiene.py` blocks feature-branch references (a merged branch is
stale in a durable catalog) and unknown status words.

| # | Title | Status | PR | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|

Adds a `sweep` verb to `scripts/intelligence/memory-janitor.py` — one bounded maintenance pass over active non-`duplicate` entries: (1) GLOBAL DETERMINISTIC enrichment (idempotent) — `dedup()` → `tag(all)` → `edges()`; (2) SLM enrichment (honest-defer per entry when the loopback router is unreachable) — `topic` + `summarize` on entries missing them (+ `extract-facts` via the extract-facts stage effect during advance; `classify` on model-mistake entries); (3) BOUNDED lifecycle advance toward STOP_STAGE=`verify` (`SOVEREIGN_OS_MEMORY_JANITOR_STOP_STAGE`, `--stop`), ONE step per tick — `stage<stop`→`advance()` (current stage effect + one label bump via memory-admit.advance, the sole `stage` owner); `stage==verify`→apply the verify effect DIRECTLY (`verified:true`) WITHOUT advancing (so it's verified but NEVER auto-`promote`d — the subtlety: advance() runs the *current* stage's effect then bumps, so stopping at verify by never-advancing-from-verify would leave the verify effect unapplied); `stage>verify`→operator-advanced, left untouched. The auto-sweep NEVER crosses into `promote`/`decay`/`archive` (value/retention judgments stay operator-gated). + a recurrent `sovereign-memory-janitor.{service,timer}` (~10-min oneshot — heavier than observe's 5-min since it makes SLM calls, R171-hardened, mirroring the SDD-069 observe units) + `scripts/hooks/recurrent/memory-janitor.sh` (sources common.sh + observability.sh; runs `janitor sweep --confirm`; emits `sovereign_os_memory_janitor_run_total{result}` + `_swept_total{result}` with fail-class symmetry) — in full lockstep with the 6 recurrent-hook registries (EXPECTED_RECURRENT_HOOKS + HOOK_TO_TIMER_SLUG + 18→19 count/prose, ongoing.md timer table + 18→19 count bumps, dashboards README metric inventory, metric-coverage EXEMPT_PATTERNS, hook-layer-B). The osctl `janitor)` arm already routes `janitor <job> "$@"` → memory-janitor.py, so `janitor sweep` routes with NO osctl change (only the arm comment/job-list updated). R10212/SB-077 PRESERVED — the sweep MUTATES the store so it is CLI/timer-ONLY, never a web control (the memory-changes-api daemon stays read-only 405); bounded advance never auto-promotes/archives; SLM jobs honest-defer (never fabricate); one owner of `stage` (delegates to memory-admit.advance); dedup marks `duplicate` + never hard-deletes; DRY-RUN default (the timer runs live); idempotent (deterministic jobs + the stop-stage guard); NO contract yaml change (the 11-stage lifecycle + admission_rules locks are untouched). | 502 | Incremental Earley parser — per-token grammar masking without re-parsing the prefix | active | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-21 (*"Good, we continue, another big PR"* → chose *"Incremental grammar parser"*). The third SDD in the control-bits band (500–599); closes the honest-perf caveat SDD-500/501 both flagged. `TokenGrammarMask::mask` re-parsed the whole prefix EACH token (`parse_chart` rebuilds a fresh Earley chart every call; `is_live_prefix` per surviving token) — ≈ O(S·L·G) per step, quadratic across a generation. Key property: the Earley chart is a PURE function of the prefix (building state k+1 only appends it, never mutates 0..=k), so a committed prefix parses once and each candidate token is validated by feed-then-rollback (cost ∝ token length, not prefix length) — bit-for-bit identical to the from-scratch recognizer. Ships (NO new crate — 722 unchanged): `EarleyChart` + `Grammar::start_chart`/`feed`/`rollback_to`/`next_set`/`is_live`/`accepts` in `sovereign-cfg-grammar`; `TokenGrammarMask::mask` rewired to the within-call incremental path (DROP-IN, exact parity — every caller `complete_json_schema`/`complete_regex`/`complete_json_schema_with_laws` inherits the speedup with zero code change, per-step cost O(S·L·G)→O(L·G + S·t·G)); and a stateful `IncrementalGrammarMask` that persists the chart across steps (`advance`/`mask`) → linear per generation. Honest boundary: the stateful masker is CHARACTER-domain and requires a char-concatenative tokenizer (byte-BPE satisfies it; merge-BPE may not), so it ships as a substrate — the LLM wiring keeps the stateless drop-in `mask`. Parity is the acceptance test (unchanged `prefilter_matches_full_check` + new EarleyChart-vs-from-scratch tests). Verified: `cargo test -p sovereign-cfg-grammar -p sovereign-token-grammar-mask` (14+14) + all downstream green (llm 79+28, json-schema 13, token-law-mask 9, decoder-stack 37 — parity inherited); clippy + fmt clean; `tests/lint/test_incremental_grammar_parser_contract.py` locks the append-only contract + the char-concatenative caveat. | 504 | Safety denylist as a negative-constraint token-law plane | active | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-21 (*"Good, we continue, another big PR"*). The fifth SDD in the control-bits band (500–599); ships the source SDD-503 explicitly deferred (§Non-goals #1 "a safety-denylist plane … needs a new text→token projection, a separate design"), completing the M00117 five-plane vision (grammar · schema · tool · SAFETY · route). Every constraint 500–503 is a POSITIVE allow-list; safety is the opposite — "the output must NEVER contain any of these substrings" (injection markers, banned phrases) — a NEGATIVE constraint. The crux: a substring ban is NOT a per-token property (a forbidden phrase spans token boundaries — with a byte tokenizer "ab" is token `a` then token `b`, neither contains "ab"). Realization: compile the denied substrings into an Aho-Corasick automaton, walk it to the committed generation's scan state, and each step ban exactly the tokens whose bytes would COMPLETE a banned match — `DenyConstraint::safe_token_ids` returns the safe allow-list (same `Vec<usize>` shape regex/grammar planes use, so it composes via `token_law_combine`). EXACT per-step guarantee (a banned phrase can only appear at the byte that finishes it → masked at that step), not a post-hoc scanner. Ships: `AcState` + `start`/`advance`/`hits` incremental scan-state API in `sovereign-aho-corasick` (its `step` was private); NEW crate `sovereign-token-law-deny` (722→723) with `DenyConstraint`/`safe_token_ids`; `complete_with_safety_denylist` + `complete_regex_with_safety_denylist` (positive regex ∧ negative denylist at once) in `sovereign-llm`. Real source: consumes `sovereign_injection_detect::PATTERNS` verbatim. Honest boundary: entropy/checksum detectors (secret-scan, pii-redact) are NOT per-token → stay post-hoc scanners, NOT planes (deliberately out of scope). | 989 | MS003 signing primitive — sovereign-os mints ed25519 (Option B, producer half) (F-2026-034) | complete | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-13 (AskUserQuestion → **"B — sovereign-os mints (recommended)"**). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Advances F-2026-034 (CRIT)** — the `unsigned-pending-MS003` placeholder every SDD-142..204 record carries. Implements the operator's Option-B choice from SDD-984: **sovereign-os mints a real ed25519 signature over each record with the operator key identity; selfdef verifies** — real signatures now, no coupling to selfdef uptime (preserves MS043 offline-survivability), R10212 untouched (signs only records sovereign-os already authors on its own authority). **PR 1 of 2 = the producer PRIMITIVE only** (crypto reviewed in isolation; PR 2 sweeps the ~8 writers). **NEW `scripts/lib/ms003.py`**: `sign(record)` → `ms003:ed25519:<keyid>:<sig>` when an operator key is present, else the historical `unsigned-pending-MS003` placeholder — **never raises** (a signing fault degrades to the placeholder, never breaks a mutation write); `verify()` (selfdef-side reference), `canonical_bytes()` (record minus `signature`, sort_keys, compact, UTF-8 — the byte contract), `is_signed()`, `keyid()`, CLI `gen-key`/`pubkey`/`status`. **NO NEW DEPENDENCY**: the `cryptography` wheel is unimportable here (`_cffi_backend` → a pyo3 `PanicException` that escapes `except Exception`), so signing shells to the **system `openssl`** (already a hard dep — SecureBoot uses it), keeping the scripts stdlib-only + locally verifiable. **Opportunistic**: a real signature needs BOTH an ed25519-capable openssl AND a key at `$SOVEREIGN_OS_MS003_KEY` (default `~/.sovereign-os/ms003.key`); a keyless node behaves EXACTLY as today → PR 2 is a no-op until a key is provisioned. **Wire format** (the contract selfdef implements): `keyid`=first 16 of base64url(raw 32-byte pubkey), `sig`=base64url(64-byte ed25519 sig), signed bytes=`canonical_bytes`; provision/export the trust anchor via `gen-key`/`pubkey`. **NEW `tests/unit/test_ms003_sign.py`** — 6 tests: no-key→placeholder, never-raises-on-garbage-key, `canonical_bytes` excludes signature + key-order-stable, placeholder-never-verifies, and (skip-if-no-ed25519) full sign→verify round-trip + tamper-reject + wrong-key-reject + gen-key-refuses-overwrite. **Verified:** `pytest tests/unit/test_ms003_sign.py` **6 passed** (real-crypto cases ran); | 990 | MS003 writer sweep — wire ms003.sign() into the 8 decision-writers (Option B, PR 2) (F-2026-034) | complete | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-13 ("MS003 implementation arc"; *"we do not minimize, we do this right"*). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Advances F-2026-034 (CRIT)** — PR 2 of the arc, consuming the SDD-989 primitive. SDD-989 shipped `scripts/lib/ms003.py` in isolation; this wires `ms003.sign()` into the **eight runtime decision/mutation writers** that until now hard-coded the `unsigned-pending-MS003` placeholder: `scripts/intelligence/{memory-store,memory-decide}.py`, `scripts/inference/{adapter-decide,adapter-gate}.py`, `scripts/lifecycle/{approval-decide,save-state,session-decide,session-runtime}.py`. Because `canonical_bytes()` **excludes the `signature` field**, leaving the pre-existing `"signature": _UNSIGNED` literal in the wrapped dict is harmless (overwritten + never in the signed bytes) — minimal diff. **Two site shapes needed care**: assignment-then-append-fields (`adapter-decide` registry entry, `approval-decide` approval record) sign **after** full assembly; mutate-in-place-then-rewrite (`memory-store` undo `reversed` flip) **re-signs** (signatures are point-in-time). Provenance spans that BORROW a decision's signature are left as-is (decision signed before emit); self-built spans are signed directly. **Graceful fallback = zero behaviour change without a key**: `sign()` returns the placeholder + never raises when no operator key, so every keyless node + every CI runner emits the identical placeholder — real signatures switch on only after `gen-key`. **NEW `tests/unit/test_ms003_writer_signing.py`** — 4 tests proving the wiring end-to-end across two families + both import styles: with a provisioned key, `memory-decide` (in-process) + `approval-decide` (subprocess) write a **durable ledger record whose signature `ms003.verify()` accepts**, tampering breaks it; keyless → placeholder. **Verified:** writer-signing 4 passed (real-crypto ran); every swept writer's suite green (memory-store 31 / memory-decide 18 / adapter-decide 20 / adapter-gate 21 / approval-decide 10 / save-state 18 / session-decide 18 / session-runtime 17); **full tests/unit 505 passed**; ruff clean. | 991 | CoAT no longer serializes generation — narrow the cortex lock to per-recall (F-2026-063/090) | complete | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-13 ("MS003 implementation arc, CoAT-through-jobs runtime fix"). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Advances F-2026-063 (MED) + F-2026-090 (OPP)** (bonus corner of F-2026-065). **Root cause**: `GatewayServer::coat()` ran the whole CoAT deliberation **holding the shared cortex mutex** — `CortexRecall` borrowed `&Cortex`, so the `MutexGuard` lived across up to **12 model-backed expansions**. `self.cortex: Mutex<Cortex>` is the SAME mutex `infer()`/`explain`/`simple`/`deliberate`/every other `/v1/coat` locks, so one model-backed CoAT **serialized all other generation** for the whole multi-second deliberation (F-2026-090's "holding the generation mutex — serially blocks all other generation"; the mechanism behind F-2026-063). `infer()` by contrast holds it only briefly (one scoped `act_and_learn`). **Fix**: `CortexRecall` now borrows the **mutex** (`&Mutex<Cortex>`), not a guard, and locks **per recall** — the same short-hold pattern `infer()` uses; `coat()` no longer pre-locks, so between the ≤12 expansions the cortex mutex is FREE and `/v1/infer` (+ every decision surface + other `/v1/coat`) interleaves instead of blocking. **Why this, not "route through jobs" alone**: `_run_deliberation` issues the SAME synchronous `POST /v1/coat`, so moving the caller to a background thread would NOT have removed the gatewayd-side lock-hold — the serialization had to be fixed IN `coat()`. (The generator mutex is still taken per model call — the correct, inherent serialization of token generation, released between expansions.) **Safety**: CoAT is read-only on cortex (recalls, never learns); per-recall locking lets a concurrent `infer()` learn BETWEEN recalls (benign — recall is advisory, freshness clock frozen at call time); the poison path now degrades to empty recall instead of panicking the request thread mid-deliberation (softer than the whole-loop `.expect()`, a nod to F-2026-065). **NEW tests**: `coat_recall_releases_the_cortex_lock_between_recalls` (after a recall `try_lock().is_ok()`) + `coat_does_not_hold_the_cortex_lock_across_deliberation` (a full heuristic `/v1/coat` leaves the mutex free). **Verified:** `cargo test -p sovereign-gatewayd` 68 lib + 18 integration passed; `cargo fmt --all --check` (CI-exact) exit 0; `cargo clippy -p sovereign-gatewayd --all-targets` clean. `crates/sovereign-gatewayd/src/lib.rs` only (private `CortexRecall` struct + `recall` + `coat`) + 2 tests — no cockpit/webapp/`scripts/operator`/crate-API change; collision-safe. **Named follow-ups (deferred)**: async caller (webapp→jobs UI steering — the request still awaits its own deliberation; contended webapp surface); model-backed integration test (needs a synthetic loadable model-dir fixture — overlaps F-2026-066). **Non-goals**: `Mutex`→`RwLock` refactor (architecturally significant, operator-level). MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. Status: SDD-991 shipped on branch. | operator-directed 2026-07-13 | SDD-991 (phase-1 audit session) |
| 992 | The gateway daemon survives a poisoned lock instead of cascading (F-2026-065) | complete | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-13 (phase-1 audit continuation). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-065 (LOW) — daemon-path half.** Every mutex access on the gateway request path used `.lock().expect("… poisoned")`. A `Mutex` is POISONED when a thread panics holding its guard, and stays poisoned — so every `.lock().expect()` after it panics too: on a root-adjacent daemon, one panicking request thread cascades to take the whole daemon down one request at a time (exactly the finding's "lock poisoning would cascade to every request"). **15 sites** across `crates/sovereign-gatewayd/src/lib.rs`: the `cortex` mutex (`infer`/`explain`/`decide`/`deliberate`/`coat`/`maintain`/`persist_memory`) + the `ledger` mutex (counters/health/metrics/Ledger response). **Fix — two guards matched to what each lock protects**: `cortex_guard()` → `Result<MutexGuard, GatewayResponse>` DECLINES a poisoned cortex (the decision engine may hold torn state from a prior mid-mutation panic) — handlers `return GatewayResponse::Error` instead of panicking (`persist_memory` maps to an I/O error; `maintain` skips the cycle, `return 0`); `ledger_guard()` RECOVERS a poisoned ledger (takes the guard through the poison via `into_inner()`) — the guarded ops are counter increments that can't tear, and dropping an already-computed response over a stat lock would be the wrong trade. **Kept as-is (per the finding)**: the two `sovereign-coat` `.expect()`s (`seeds non-empty`, `non-root on best path`) are pure-lib invariant guards, not daemon lock state — the finding says keep pure-lib expects; untouched. **NEW tests** (poison a mutex the real way — a thread panics holding the guard, stderr silenced): `cortex_guard_declines_a_poisoned_lock_instead_of_panicking`, `infer_on_a_poisoned_cortex_returns_error_not_panic` (end-to-end), `ledger_guard_recovers_a_poisoned_lock_and_keeps_serving`. **Verified:** `cargo test -p sovereign-gatewayd` 71 lib + 4 + 18 integration passed (was 68 lib; +3); `cargo fmt --all --check` (CI-exact) exit 0; `cargo clippy -p sovereign-gatewayd --all-targets` clean. gatewayd-crate only (2 private helpers + 15 call-site conversions + 3 tests) — no coat/cockpit/webapp/`scripts/operator`/crate-API change; collision-safe; no new dependency. **Non-goals**: the coat pure-lib expects (kept); making the guarded ops themselves panic-free (this bounds the blast radius to one declined request); broader unwrap/expect audits. MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. Status: SDD-992 shipped on branch. | operator-directed 2026-07-13 | SDD-992 (phase-1 audit session) |

| 710 | Enforce the `unsafe` ban at compile time across all 202 cockpit crates (F-2026-096) | draft | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-14 (*"lets do a big round"* — phase-1 audit continuation). **Band 700–799 per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-096 (MED); makes F-2026-004's "all inherit workspace lints" claim fully true.** `sovereign-os` treats "no `unsafe` outside the sanctioned AVX-512 carve-out (`sovereign-simd`)" as a core safety invariant, and the root `[workspace.lints.rust]` declares `unsafe_code = "forbid"` — but a crate inherits that lint only if it declares `[lints] workspace = true`. The audit (SDD-974) found **202 of 717 crates** (the whole `sovereign-cockpit-*` family) declared **no `[lints]` table**, so the compiler would not stop a future `unsafe` in them; the ban rested on a CI grep alone (`test_workspace_hygiene_baseline.py` invariant 6). (2) `test_workspace_hygiene_baseline.py` gains invariant 7 (2 cases): every member crate must declare `[lints] workspace = true` except the carve-out (a NEW crate that forgets it now fails CI — the exact F-2026-096 gap), and the carve-out must declare its `unsafe_code = "allow"` explicitly (auditable, not an omitted table); invariant 6's grep is retained as defence-in-depth. **Provably safe**: `unsafe_code=forbid` is inert (none of the 202 use unsafe), `missing_docs=warn` can't fail a build, and `[workspace.lints.clippy]` is all-`allow` (inheriting it only relaxes clippy). **Verified:** census 716+1+0=717; every swept manifest re-parses; `cargo metadata` OK; `cargo check -p sovereign-cockpit-accent-color-policy` clean under inherited lints; baseline lint 8 passed (6+2); full `tests/` + 5 profiles + ruff green. **Non-goals**: the cockpit-consolidation question (F-2026-001, architectural); changing the simd carve-out. | 701 | NVIDIA GPU bring-up — install the pinned ≥570 driver + apply the power caps at boot (F-2026-109..110) | draft | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-14 (build-and-flash readiness review — GPU bring-up; driver channel chosen: CUDA-repo-pinned `.run` ≥570). **Band 700–799 (phase-1 audit continuation) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-109 (HIGH) + F-2026-110 (MED).** **F-2026-109**: the profile bakes `nvidia-open-kernel-dkms`+`nvidia-driver`, but trixie ships 550.163 which predates the Blackwell GB202 (RTX PRO 6000 Max-Q + RTX 5090) — the profile itself notes the ≥570 driver must come at first boot, and NOTHING installed it (`nvidia-driver-bind.sh` only blacklists nouveau). Everything else stays non-fatal. **Verified:** `bash -n` both scripts clean; `pytest test_build_pipeline_verbatim.py test_shell_safety_flags.py test_graceful_shutdown_contract.py` 32 passed; full `tests/lint` green. 2 build scripts + SDD-999 + INDEX/mandate/CHANGELOG/ledger/catalog/context — no crate/gatewayd/cockpit/webapp change; no new dependency; all 9 step scripts already exist + the normal bake creates the operator + enables the target, so the stricter defaults don't break the current build (VM path leaves `BAKE_FIRSTBOOT` unset → §6 skipped); collision-safe. **Non-goals**: making optional provisioning steps fatal (they degrade by design); DKMS-failure surfacing (Batch 3 GPU SDD); re-architecting the step/state/resume model. | 994 | The inference router bounds the request body instead of crashing / over-allocating (F-2026-097) | complete | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-14 (phase-1 audit continuation, *"we continue"*). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-097 (LOW).** `scripts/inference/router.py` `_do_post_inner` read the POST body as `length = int(self.headers.get("Content-Length", 0)); raw = self.rfile.read(length)` — two defects on the OpenAI-compatible front door: (1) a non-numeric `Content-Length` raised an **uncaught `ValueError`** (handler crash + dropped connection; the `0` default only covers an *absent* header, not garbage); (2) `rfile.read(length)` trusted the client length **unbounded** (a huge value forces an unbounded allocation — memory-DoS). Every sibling operator daemon (`control-exec-api` `_MAX_BODY`, `code-console-api` `length<=0 or >64_000`, `brain-api` try/except) already guarded both; the router was the outlier. **Fix**: a pure `parse_content_length(raw, max_body=_MAX_BODY) -> (length, error)` — absent/empty → `(0,None)`; malformed/negative → `400`; oversize → `413`; valid ≤ cap → the length; `_do_post_inner` rejects (`send_error(*err)`) before reading. Cap is a generous **16 MiB** (the router proxies inference requests — long-context prompts are legitimately large — vs the 64 KB tiny-control cap). **NEW `tests/unit/test_router_body_bounds.py`** (11 cases: absent/empty → 0; valid + at-cap pass; non-numeric / whitespace-garbage / negative → 400; cap+1 and a 1 TiB claim → 413 before any read; custom `max_body` boundary). **Verified:** `pytest tests/unit/test_router_body_bounds.py tests/unit/test_router_classify.py tests/unit/test_router_scheduler_advisory.py` **42 passed** (11 new + 31 existing router tests unchanged); `ruff check` clean. `scripts/inference/router.py` only (1 constant + 1 pure helper + a 2-line call-site change) + 1 new test + this SDD + registries — no cockpit/webapp/crate/other-daemon change; collision-safe; no new dependency; R10212/MS043 untouched. **Non-goals**: a shared `BaseOperatorHandler` unifying the ~58 hand-rolled body-read handlers (F-2026-093 island theme — this closes the one crash/DoS outlier); chunked-transfer bodies; per-deployment cap tuning. | 954 | Auto-mode permission classifier — flag normalization + honest "best-effort UX, not a boundary" framing | draft | post-Gate-5 | Operator-directed 2026-07-12 (*"go"* — Phase-1 audit). **Band 950–999 (general/audit session) per SDD-100.** Closes ledger **F-2026-092**. The Auto-mode safety classifier (`scripts/operator/lib/permission_classifier.py`) had (1) an **evadable `rm` pattern** — a single combined-token regex that only matched recursive+force flags written *together* (`rm -rf`), so `rm -r -f /x` (split) and `rm -R -f /x` (uppercase) **escaped** `destructive` and fell to `confirm`, undercutting Auto's job to block the recursive-delete class; and (2) it was **mis-framed as a boundary** despite being an evadable heuristic denylist. **`permission_classifier.py`**: the two `rm` regexes replaced by `_rm_recursive_or_force(cmd)` — finds any `rm` token (basename, so `sudo rm …` counts), scans its option tokens (stopping flag-collection at `--`), and flags recursive (`-r`/`-R`/`--recursive`) OR force (`-f`/`--force`) across split/combined/reordered/uppercase/long forms → `destructive`; `classify()` calls it before the regex loop. Fail-safe preserved (unrecognized/obfuscated → `unknown` → confirm, never silent-allow) + tightening-only (nothing that blocked/confirmed becomes allow). Module docstring + the plan-mode directive **reframed**: best-effort UX heuristic, NOT a security boundary — the real boundary is the allowlisted execute daemon (`control-exec-api`) + fs sandbox (F-2026-081); a `block` = "spared the operator a mistake", not "an attacker was stopped". NEW `docs/sdd/954-permission-classifier-flag-normalization.md`. **Verified:** `python3 -m pytest tests/lint/test_plan_mode_contract.py` 7 (2 new — every `rm` recursive/force arrangement → destructive/block, `rm file.txt` → confirm fail-safe, module+directive framed best-effort-not-boundary); `ruff check` clean; full `tests/lint` green. **Non-goals**: defeating quoting/`$IFS`/base64 obfuscation (a regex can't — the fail-safe direction already prevents silent-allow); the real boundary = sandbox/fs-enforcement around execution paths (F-2026-081). | 149 | dashboard serve.py --once: fix the empty-reply race (killed daemon worker) | complete | post-Gate-5 | test_dashboard.sh failed 2/33 (curl GET / + GET /api/health → rc=52 empty reply) — CI layer-3 nspawn gate red on PR #118. Deterministic + pre-existing on main, masked until SDD-148 fixed test_trinity (the layer-3 job stops at the first failing test; trinity failed first so dashboard never ran). Operator: "still failing". Recover band (SDD-149/E11.M149 per SDD-100). Root cause: serve.py runs ThreadingHTTPServer; for --once it calls handle_request(), which dispatches the request to a worker thread and returns as soon as the thread is spawned (NOT when the response is written); ThreadingHTTPServer workers are daemons by default, so main() reaching finally: server_close() + returning kills the worker mid-render before it flushes → empty reply. Deterministic because the full-page render (gather_all ~40 cards, 3-4s) is always still in flight; auth passes on loopback (not involved); --render-only always worked (no server). Fix: in the --once branch set srv.daemon_threads=False so server_close() (block_on_close) joins the worker and the response completes before exit; serve_forever() (normal path) untouched. Serving-lifecycle only — no route/data/auth/render change; R10212/SB-077 untouched. Verified: test_dashboard.sh 35/35 (was 31/33; success-path assertions now run too), 3/3 runs, 0 curl fails; all 7 dashboard nspawn suites green (auth 14/14, grid 21/21, intel_cards 10/10, mobile 10/10, model_detail 13/13, modules_form 0-fail); full pytest lint suite green. MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. Status: SDD-149 shipped on branch (stacked with SDD-147/148 on PR #118). | operator-directed 2026-07-11 | SDD-149 (recover-projects session) |

## Slots reserved for Stage 2 onwards (preview, non-binding)

Subsequent SDDs (011+) cover Stage 2 build scripts, lifecycle management,
first-login assistant, inference-backend stack selection (Q-017), etc.
Numbering continues monotonically; specific titles land when their PR
opens.

## How to add an SDD

1. Pick the next free three-digit number.
2. Create `docs/sdd/NNN-<short-slug>.md`.
3. Open with the canonical status block:
   ```
   > Status: <draft | review | accepted | implemented | abandoned>
   > Owner: <name or team>
   > Last updated: <YYYY-MM-DD>
   > Closes findings: F-NNNN-MMM, ...   (or "none")
   > Derived from: <upstream artifacts>
   ```
4. Sections: Mission · Problem · Required coverage · Goals · Non-goals ·
   Open questions (Q-X rows) · Way forward · Cross-references.
5. Update this INDEX with the new row.
6. When the SDD's open questions resolve, append `D-NNN` entries to
   `docs/decisions.md` and annotate the SDD's `Q-X` rows in place with
   `**answered (D-NNN, YYYY-MM-DD)**`.
